### Post by K.Mandla on 2008-06-30
**Rules:**
[INDENT][LIST=1]
[*]Forum guidelines on content apply. In other words, safe for kids and safe for work.

[*]Try not to quote embedded images; take a moment to snip them out.

[*]Off-topic posts will be edited or moved.

[*]Thumbnail your image, or use the forum's attachment system. Full-size embedded images are annoying and will be snipped mercilessly.

[*]Take a moment and tell everyone the details of your desktop, such as the theme name, the wallpaper name, the icons and any programs you're using in the image.
[/LIST][/INDENT]
Enjoy!

That looks better, but if you want a light setup you haven't used, I use this one on my desktop:

gtk theme: [murrinna dreamy]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/show.php?content=63623&vote=good&tan=13910393")
icon theme: [HH]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/HH-ubuntu?content=79580")
emerald: [embarrassingly simple]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Embarassingly+Simple?content=75531")
and the [linux mint menu]("http://linuxowns.wordpress.com/2008/06/03/install-the-linux-mint-menu-in-ubuntu-hardy/")

This is what it looks like: 

[[img]http://xs228.xs.to/xs228/08264/screenshot739.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs228&d=08264&f=screenshot739.png)

### Post by Tiede on 2008-07-01
I just made this last night... I was growing tired of my "dark and gloomy" gray June desktop...
It's supposed to be all daring, chic, and RED...
(not obnoxiously red, though...)
My only problem with this is the ***UGLY*** gnome-panel that i need for the notification area. I tried stalonetray, but it doesn't work well with metacity and makes gnome-session-save complain every time I log out.

And guess what? My card doesn't even support 3D acceleration! It's a cheap Sis Graphics Card in an Acer Aspire 3003WLMi... Thank you metacity composite!!!

My theme details:
GTK: Unity (modified to a redish color)
Metacity:Mirage-SELECTED
Icons:HumanElephant-Savane
Wallpaper:Ubuntu-supergirl modified in gimp - grayed out some parts.
Fonts: (in that order) Utopia Italic | Dustisimo Roman Italic | Ubuntu-title bold italic | Beryluim bold Italic | moonospace
AWN with the glass theme and modified color (red)

EDIT: I made a small change of the color in AWN to better match the GTK color, but the change is so subtle, only paranoid observers like me would notice. It was just a little too red...
Since it is not that big of a deal, I have decided not to reload anything for that... I'll leave it to your imagination to wonder what it is now ;)

---

how do you close windows with that theme?

### Post by Koori23 on 2008-07-02
I suspect dbbolton has edited his rc.xml file to include a keyboard shortcut to complete that task. 

If you're using XFCE or GNOME (Even Windows), Alt+F4 is the shortcut key to close the active window. It's included by default.

---

### Post by el mariachi on 2008-07-02
I don't use a lot of my mouse buttons (Razor DiamondBack) it would be to assign some of them to do this

---

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-07-02
> **el mariachi said:**
> how do you close windows with that theme?
Like Koori23 said, the default keybinding to close a window in Openbox is Alt+F4. Many applications (Thunar, Epiphany, Quod Libet) can be closed with Ctrl+W. Also, many apps can be closed with Ctrl+Q (Firefox, Pidgin). You can usually find "Close" or "Quit" under the "File" menu too. A final option is to middle-click on the window's task list entry in pypanel.

---

### Post by Ioky on 2008-07-03
This is the Desktop for my only laptop: Gundam Black

Xfce
GTK: wii-black
theme: wii-black
icon: final order
conky (modify from [this]("http://blog.brixandersen.dk/?p=67"))
A gundam wing wallpaper mono / modify the hue with gimp
a modify launch button

The system is pretty old, but it doesn't mean it can't be cool. My goal is keep the system as light as possible so I didn't use compiz and screenlets. Instead I use conky to build up the coolness of the Desktop. 

BTW: there is a down side of this setting, it is that because it is xfce, if you use a full desktop cover conky like that, icons on the desktop will be disappear. Which in this case it doesn't effect me much because I do really save anything on my desktop and make it messy, but for some people, they might think it is a bit annoying. If you use gnome, that shouldn't be a problem though.

----------------------------------------

Also, since other people here use compiz, would anyone been able to explain to me if it's possible to change on which borders you can resize an emerald window?

I like using my scrollwheel to shade windows but half the time I try to do it, it doesn't work because my mouse pointer is too close to the top edge of the window frame and when the mouse pointer turns into the little up-arrow, indicating that you can resize the window, it prevents the mousewheel from having any effect. 

With Xfwm4, you could resize a window starting from any edge *other* than the top one, presumably to prevent this issue.

Edit: It's also annoying that I accidentally resize a window whenever I try to simply bloody move it.

### Post by joninkrakow on 2008-07-05
This is my first attempt to upload. We'll see how it goes.

I don't think there's anything spectacular about my desktop, but there are a couple elements to it. 

This is LXDE, running icewm as its WM. The icewm theme may be familiar to some here--it's the ThinBlack theme that is posted here on these forums. I was happy with the default Openbox theme for LXDE, but really like the thin, reflective title bar and wide window borders on ThinBlack, hence the change to icewm and this theme. :-) Thanks to whoever made it. I doubt I will be changing any time soon.

Vital stats summary:

DE: LXDE
WM: icewm
GTK theme: Clearlooks
icons: Elementary
fonts: standard
Wall: standard, decent-enough-looking LXDE wallpaper (since I seldom see it, thanks to FF, why bother changing it?)

-Jon

P.S. Why doesn't the avatar pic I uploaded show? I can't make it show up. :-(

### Post by MaxIBoy on 2008-07-10
Video of my eye candy settings:
[http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iIuMJ_hWgvI&feature=user](http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iIuMJ_hWgvI&feature=user)

Screenshots of my theme are in an attachment. In the bigger one, the two windows are just file browsers.


My theme is custom. Window borders are crux, icons are Tangerine, and controls are Crux. As for colors, window backgrounds are 230 red, 230 green, and 230 blue, input boxes are white, selected items are 252 red, 52 green, and 0 blue, tooltips are 255 red, 255 green and 0 blue. All text is black. The pointer is DMZ-White.


My desktop background was found in a google image search for "ubuntu flames." I'm not actually using the satanic edition.

### Post by easybake on 2008-07-10
> **masterlotep said:**
> Nice desktop.Details please.

Cairo-Dock

Futurelooks theme: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=796572&highlight=futurelooks]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=796572&highlight=futurelooks")

Wallpaper: [http://swaroop.deviantart.com/art/moon-magick-9174464]("http://swaroop.deviantart.com/art/moon-magick-9174464")

Rainlendar skin: [http://customize.org/rainlendar/skins/57943]("http://customize.org/rainlendar/skins/57943")(its not really in spanish)

Some Icons photoshopped from this set:[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/BuuF-Deuce-iconset?content=46201]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/BuuF-Deuce-iconset?content=46201")

Conkys

Time Conky:
```
#background yes

font freesans:size=8
xftfont freesans:size=8
use_xft yes

xftalpha 1

update_interval 5.0

own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes

double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
minimum_size 165 55

color0 ffffff
color1 cbcbcb
color2 a6a6a6
color3 919191
color4 757575
color5 000000

draw_outline no

draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no

default_color grey90

default_outline_color DarkGrey

#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

gap_x 0
gap_y 0

no_buffers yes

uppercase no

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
    ${color0}${font impact:style=Bold:pixelsize=60}${time %I:%M}
```
System Conky
```

use_spacer yes

#background yes

font freesans:size=8
xftfont freesans:size=8
use_xft yes

xftalpha 1

update_interval 5.0

own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes

double_buffer yes
draw_shades yes
minimum_size 230 5
maximum_width 140

color0 ffffff
color1 ffffff
color2 ffffff
color3 ffffff
color4 ffffff
color5 ffffff

draw_outline no
default_shade_color 404040

draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no

default_color grey90

default_outline_color DarkGrey

#alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
alignment bottom_right

gap_x 10
gap_y 10

no_buffers yes

uppercase no

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
$hr
${voffset -1}CPU$alignc       $processes$alignr$cpu%
${voffset -6}$hr
${cpugraph 60,140 192D5B 2C4D9B}

${voffset -71}  ${color1}${top name 1} $alignr${top cpu 1}  
  ${color2}${top name 2}$alignr${top cpu 2}  
  ${color3}${top name 3}$alignr${top cpu 3}  
  ${color3}${top name 4}$alignr${top cpu 4}  

$hr
${voffset -1}${color5}RAM$alignr$memperc%
${voffset -6}$hr

${voffset -6}  ${color1}${top_mem name 1} $alignr${top_mem mem 1}  
  ${color2}${top_mem name 2}$alignr${top_mem mem 2}  
  ${color3}${top_mem name 3}$alignr${top_mem mem 3}  
  ${color3}${top_mem name 4}$alignr${top_mem mem 4}  

$hr
${voffset -1}HD$alignr$fs_free_perc%
${voffset -6}$hr
  ${color5}${fs_used}${color1} $alignr${fs_free} 

$hr
${voffset -1}${color2}GMail:$font$alignr${color1}${texeci 100 python gmail.py}
${voffset -6}$hr
${color #29F301}${shadecolor}${upspeedgraph eth0 60,69 03648E 01B2FE}${color #178600}$alignr${shadecolor}${downspeedgraph eth0 60,69 9F0000 D20101}

${shadecolor 000000}${voffset -72}${color0}UP$alignr${color0}DOWN

${color2}${upspeed eth0}k/s$alignr$font${color2}${downspeed eth0}k/s
${color2}${totalup eth0}$alignr${totaldown eth0}
${shadecolor 000000}${color 000000}$hr
```
Weather Conky:
```

#background yes

font freesans:size=8
xftfont freesans:size=8
use_xft yes

xftalpha 1

update_interval 100.0

own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes

double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
minimum_size 140
maximum_width 500

color0 ffffff
color1 cbcbcb
color2 000000
color3 919191
color4 757575
color5 ffffff

draw_outline no

draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no

default_color grey90

default_outline_color DarkGrey

#alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
alignment bottom_right

gap_x 10
gap_y 355

no_buffers yes

uppercase no

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
$hr
${voffset -1}Mundelein, IL
${voffset -6}$hr

${voffset -3}  ${font arial:style=Bold:size=20}${color0}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=HT -i -u}$font$alignr${color1}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=CC --startday=0}

${voffset -4}$hr
  ${color0}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=DW --startday=1 -w}$alignr${color3}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=HT --startday=1 -i -u}/${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=LT --startday=1 -i -u}
  ${color0}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=DW --startday=2 -w}$alignr${color3}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=HT --startday=2 -i -u}/${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=LT --startday=2 -i -u}
  ${color0}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=DW --startday=3 -w}$alignr${color3}${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=HT --startday=3 -i -u}/${execi 3600 python conkyforecast.py --location=USIL0823 --datatype=LT --startday=3 -i -u}
```

### Post by 71CH on 2008-07-11
> **Sealbhach said:**
> Could we see the conky details?
.

Sure

```
use_xft yes
xftfont verdana:size=8
alignment top_right
double_buffer yes
# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

TEXT
${color1}$hr
${voffset -3}$alignc CURRENT CONDITIONS
${voffset -7}$hr $color
$alignc Edison, New Jersey

${execi 900 perl ~/.scripts/weather.pl USNJ0131 f w}
${voffset -30}$alignr${offset -50}${execi 900 perl ~/.scripts/weather.pl USNJ0131 f t}

${font weather:size=45}${execi 900 perl ~/.scripts/weather.pl USNJ0131 f cp}$font
${voffset -7}$hr $color
$alignc Seoul, South Korea

${execi 900 perl ~/.scripts/weather2.pl KSXX0037 f w}
${voffset -30}$alignr${offset -50}${execi 900 perl ~/.scripts/weather2.pl KSXX0037 f t}

${font weather:size=45}${execi 900 perl ~/.scripts/weather2.pl KSXX0037 f cp}$font
${voffset -10}${color1}$hr

${font weather:size=28}x ${font}HDD ${execi 1 ~/.scripts/hddmonit.sh}°C 
    
${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}v${font}   Up. ${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s 
${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}r${font}   Dow. ${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s 

${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}M${font}   Upload. ${totalup wlan0}
${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}S${font}   Download. ${totaldown wlan0}
   
${font StyleBats:size=18}A${font}   CPU Average:  ${cpu}%
${font StyleBats:size=18}A${font}   CPU1 ${cpu cpu1}% ${cpubar cpu1}
${font StyleBats:size=18}A${font}   CPU2 ${cpu cpu2}% ${cpubar cpu2}

${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}J${font}   $mem / $memmax

${font StyleBats:size=18}P${font}   Work:  ${uptime_short}
${font StyleBats:size=18}4${font}   ${time %A %d %B}

${font xspiralmental:size=17}E${font}   ${kernel}
```

This conky also needs scripts to work.  Let me know if you want them.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-07-11
> **el mariachi said:**
> have those themes been released?

If you were referring to mine, you can get the GTK theme here: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/NodokaOrangeBlack?content=75186](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/NodokaOrangeBlack?content=75186) (I modified the colors slightly)

You can get the Openbox theme here: [http://box-look.org/content/show.php?content=85035](http://box-look.org/content/show.php?content=85035)

> **fedex1993 said:**
> what is the bar at the top and bottom and if they have config files can i have them please :)
The bar at the top is pypanel, and the one at the bottom is tint2 ( [http://code.google.com/p/tint2/](http://code.google.com/p/tint2/) )

My ~/.pypanelrc file:
```

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#
#                         PyPanel v2.4 Configuration
#
# This configuration file is a Python script that will be executed when
# PyPanel is started.  In order for PyPanel to start properly, make sure that
# this file contains proper Python formatting and no syntax errors.
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
VERSION         = 2.4           # Config file version

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Colors: Format is hex triplet - 0xrrggbb
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
BG_COLOR        = "0x262626"    # Panel background and tinting color
TASK_COLOR      = "0x262626"    # Normal task name color 
FOCUSED_COLOR   = "0x262626"    # Focused task name color
SHADED_COLOR    = "0x262626"    # Shaded task name color 
MINIMIZED_COLOR = "0x262626"    # Minimized task name color 
DESKTOP_COLOR   = "0xf57900"    # Desktop name color
CLOCK_COLOR     = "0xf0f0f0"    # Clock text color
LINE_COLOR      = "0xeaeaea"    # Vertical line color

# Text Shadow Colors
TASK_SHADOW_COLOR      = "0xffffff"
FOCUSED_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
SHADED_SHADOW_COLOR    = "0xffffff"
MINIMIZED_SHADOW_COLOR = "0xffffff" 
DESKTOP_SHADOW_COLOR   = "0xffffff"
CLOCK_SHADOW_COLOR     = "0xffffff"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Spacing and Location Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
P_LOCATION      = 0           # Panel placement: 0 = top, 1 = bottom
P_WIDTH         = 0            # Panel width: 0 = Use full screen width
P_START         = 0             # Starting X coordinate of the panel
P_SPACER        = 12             # Spacing between panel objects
P_HEIGHT        = 32            # Panel height

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Icon Size Options: Measured in pixels
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I_HEIGHT        = 24            # Panel application icon height
I_WIDTH         = 24          # Panel application icon Width 
APPL_I_HEIGHT   = 24            # Application launcher icon height
APPL_I_WIDTH    = 24          # Application launcher icon width
TRAY_I_HEIGHT   = 24           # System tray icon height (usually 16 or 24)
TRAY_I_WIDTH    = 24          # System tray icon width  (usually 16 or 24)
                                # If TRAY_I_WIDTH is set to 0, then the
                                # width specified by the tray app will be used
                                
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Clock Format: 'man strftime' for detailed formatting options and help
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_FORMAT    = "%a %d %b, %l:%M %p"  #%Y-%m-%d %H:%M"    # Ex: 2004-09-25 17:45 

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Clock Delay: Seconds between each clock update during periods of inactivity
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
CLOCK_DELAY     = 1

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Application List: Apps listed here will not be display on the panel
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
# Ex: ["xmms", "xine", "gDesklets"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDE_LIST       = ["gmrun",]            
                   
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Hidden Panel Size: Size of the panel when it's hidden/minimized
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
HIDDEN_SIZE     = 2

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Text Font: This option takes either a traditional or Xft font string 
# Ex: "-schumacher-clean-medium-r-normal-*-12-*-*-*-*-*-*-*"
#     "aquafont-8" 
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
FONT            = "myriadpro-9"

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show All Applications: Show apps from all desktops or just the current
# 0: Disabled - Only applications on the current desktop will be displayed
# 1: Enabled  - Selected apps are moved to the current desktop
# 2: Enabled  - Current desktop is changed to the selected apps desktop
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWALL         = 0             # 0, 1 or 2 - see descriptions above

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Show Minimized/Iconified Applications: Show only minimized apps or all apps
# 0: Disabled - Show all applications on the panel
# 1: Enabled  - Show only minimized apps on the panel
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHOWMINIMIZED   = 0

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Icon List: List of custom icons for specific applications
# The application name is its WM_CLASS name, use 'xprop' to find WM_CLASS
#
# The "default" entry is used for applications with no icon.  If left "",
# PyPanel will use the default icon distributed with the source.
#
# Add entries using the following format -
#     "<application name>" : "<full path to icon>",
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ICON_LIST       = {
                   "default" : "",
                   "example" : "/usr/share/imlib2/data/images/audio.png",
                  }
                  
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Application Launch List: Ordered list of icons and applications for the
#                          application launcher.
# 
# Add entries using the following format -
#     ("<executable>", "<full path to icon>")
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
LAUNCH_LIST     = [
                   ("xdotool key ctrl+alt+q", "/home/daniel/Art/obmenu.png"), 
                   #("leafpad", "/home/daniel/.icons/nuoveXT.2.1/16x16/apps/text-editor.png"),
                   #("firefox", "/home/daniel/.icons/nuoveXT.2.1/16x16/apps/mozilla-firefox.png"),
                   #("gaim", "/usr/share/icons/Tango/16x16/apps/gaim.png"),
                   #("exaile", "/home/daniel/.icons/nuoveXT.2.1/16x16/apps/exaile.png"),
                   #("thunar /home/daniel", "/home/daniel/Art/start-here-48.png")
                  ]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Background Alpha/Shade Level: 0 (Fully Translucent) -> 255 (Fully Opaque)
# BG_COLOR is used for tinting
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SHADE           = 255

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Misc. Options: 1 = Enabled/Yes, 0 = Disabled/No
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
ABOVE           = 0             # Panel is always above other apps
APPICONS        = 0             # Show application icons
AUTOHIDE        = 0             # Autohide uses the CLOCK_DELAY timer above
SHADOWS         = 0             # Show text shadows
SHOWLINES       = 0             # Show object seperation lines
SHOWBORDER      = 0             # Show a border around the panel

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Desktop Names: Configure the names of your desktops
# If the option is [], PyPanel will attempt to use the desktop name specified
# by the XServer, if that fails it will use the desktop number as its name
# Ex. ["One", "Two", "Three", "Four", "Five", "Six", "Seven", "Eight"]
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP_NAMES   = ["[1]", "[2]", "[3]", "[4]"]

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Panel Layout:       -----------------------------------
#                     [  1  ][  2  ][  3  ][  4  ][  5  ]
#                     -----------------------------------
#
# The panel layout is split into 5 sections numbered 1, 2, 3, 4 or 5 as shown
# in the diagram above.  Each of the following objects can be enabled by
# assigning it a section number or disabled by assigning it 0:
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
DESKTOP         = 5            # Desktop name section
TASKS           = 2           # Task names section 
TRAY            = 3           # System tray section
CLOCK           = 4            # Clock section
LAUNCHER        = 1            # Application launcher section

#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#                       Button Event Function Definitions
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Left click   - button 1 
# Middle click - button 2
# Right click  - button 3
# Wheel up     - button 4
# Wheel down   - button 5 
#
# changeDesktop(x)
# - Change Desktop: Increase or decrease the current desktop by 'x' amount
# 
# toggleShade(task)
# - Shade or Unshade an application
#
# toggleHidden()
# - Minimize the panel to the top or bottom depending on its start location
#
# toggleMinimize(task, traise=1)
# - Minimize or Unminimize an application and optionally raise it
#
# taskRaise(task, focus=1)
# - Raise an application to the top of the window list and optionally focus it 
#
# taskLower(task, focus=0)
# - Lower an app to the bottom of the window list and optionally focus it
#
# taskFocus(task)
# - Give focus to the selected application, if it has focus then minimize it
#
# showDesktop()
# - Toggle between hiding and unhiding ALL applications
#------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#----------------------------------
def desktopButtonEvent(pp, button):
#----------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's desktop object """
        
    if button == 1:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
    elif button == 2:
        pp.changeDesktop(2)
    elif button == 3:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.changeDesktop(1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.changeDesktop(-1)
        
#--------------------------------
def clockButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's clock object """
    
    if button == 1:
        os.system("xclock &")
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pp.toggleHidden()  
    elif button == 4:
        pp.showDesktop()
    elif button == 5:
        pp.showDesktop()
        
#--------------------------------
def panelButtonEvent(pp, button):
#--------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel with no active tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pass
    elif button == 2:
        pass
    elif button == 3:
        pass
    elif button == 4:
        pass
    elif button == 5:
        pass
        
#-------------------------------------
def taskButtonEvent(pp, button, task):
#-------------------------------------
    """ Button event handler for the panel's tasks """
    
    if button == 1:
        pp.taskFocus(task)
    elif button == 2:
        # Destroy the application
        task.obj.destroy()
    elif button == 3:
        # Ex. - XMMS doesn't shade, so we want to minimize it instead and
        #       still use button 3 to shade other applications
        #       task.tclass is the tasks class name (WM_CLASS)
        if "xmms" in task.tclass:
            pp.toggleMinimize(task)
        else:
            pp.toggleShade(task)
    elif button == 4:
        pp.taskRaise(task, focus=1)
    elif button == 5:
        pp.taskLower(task, focus=0)


```and my ~/.config/tint/tintrc file:

```

#---------------------------------------------
# TTM CONFIG FILE
#
# colors: hex format
# booleans: 0 or 1 
# alpha: 0 to 100 percent
# font: [FAMILY-LIST] [STYLE-OPTIONS] [SIZE]
# panel_width: 0 == use full width
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# FONT
#---------------------------------------------
font = myriad pro 10
font_color = #ececec
font_alpha = 50
font_active_color = #ffffff
font_active_alpha = 95
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
# panel_position : bottom left, bottom right, bottom center, top left, top right, top center
# panel_show_all_desktop = 0 : tint show one taskbar from current desktop
# panel_show_all_desktop = 1 : tint show all taskbar
#---------------------------------------------
panel_show_all_desktop = 1
panel_width = 1100
panel_height = 30
panel_margin = 3
panel_position = bottom center

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND
#---------------------------------------------
panel_background = 1
panel_background_color = #000000
panel_background_alpha = 50
panel_border_width = 1
panel_border_color = #ffffff
panel_border_alpha = 10
panel_rounded = 6

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 275
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 3
task_icon = 1
task_icon_size = 16

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_background = 1
task_background_color = #ffffff
task_background_alpha = 5

task_active_background_color = #e6e6e6
task_active_background_alpha = 30

task_border_width = 1
task_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_border_alpha = 5

task_rounded = 12

task_active_border_width = 1
task_active_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_active_border_alpha = 15
task_active_rounded = 16

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION
# configure mouse action with
# (none, close, toggle, iconify, shade, toggle_iconify)
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

```

### Post by PrimoTurbo on 2008-07-12
[[IMG]http://img242.imageshack.us/img242/2573/archinvirtualboxsu7.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img242.imageshack.us/my.php?image=archinvirtualboxsu7.jpg)

I got Arch running in a VirtualBox with Windows XP. This is all on a 1.6Ghz system with 768 DDR RAM. I'm suprised on how stright forward everything is, every issue I had was due to something with VirtualBox like installing Guest Additions (I forgot to type mount /media/cdrom at some point and spent hours figuring it out). Then I had no sound, guess what VirtualBox sets sound off by default with the null setting, I spent at least 3 hours trying to break Arch figuring this out, it had nothing to do with arch. Anyways this was just a test run, I will be putting it on my system soon enough along with Ubuntu & Windows.

Also I can run perfect video playback with nearly no slowdowns in VirtualBox, I didn't think it was possible. 

Running default, openbox & lxpanel with conky.

### Post by Execute_Method on 2008-07-13
> **urukrama said:**
> Where did you get that brown picture (of the building)? Do you know where that building is?

It's the Chateau de Mirinda:

During the French Revolution, the family of the Count of Liedekerke-Beaufort left the feudal castle Château de Vêves and lived at a nearby farm. After the Revolution, this opulent residence was built as a summer home for the family in 1866 by the English architect Milner, although he died before seeing its completion. The Château de Mirinda, as it was called then, was owned and used by the family except when it was briefly occupied by the Nazis in World War II. In 1958, it was used by the SNCB (a Belgian national rail company) as a home for the railwaymen's children and became Château de Noisy.

It was abandoned in 1991 and has been falling into ruins. The building has 550 windows and a clocktower that is 183 feet (56 meters) tall.


And Here's the wallpaper for ya:

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-07-13
> **Lux_Deluxe said:**
> small update

[[IMG]http://img3.imagebanana.com/img/0n7b893c/thumb/Bildschirmfoto.png[/IMG]]("http://luxdeluxe.deviantart.com/art/Desktop-Screenshot-2008-08-12-91533184")
sieht sehr gut aus ;)

> **What is in a name? said:**
> In my case, when I tried to compile it, there's always a complaint about /etc/xdg/tint/tintrc not being a valid directory, or something... Any thoughts?
I think this is the file containing tint's global/default settings. Try creating the directory then adding this to the tintrc file:

```

#---------------------------------------------
# TTM CONFIG FILE
#
# colors: hex format
# booleans: 0 or 1 
# alpha: 0 to 100 percent
# font: [FAMILY-LIST] [STYLE-OPTIONS] [SIZE]
# panel_width: 0 == use full width
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# FONT
#---------------------------------------------
font = sans 7
font_color = #ffffff
font_alpha = 55
font_active_color = #ffffff
font_active_alpha = 85
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
# panel_position : bottom left, bottom right, bottom center, top left, top right, top center
# panel_show_all_desktop = 0 : tint show one taskbar from current desktop
# panel_show_all_desktop = 1 : tint show all taskbar
#---------------------------------------------
panel_show_all_desktop = 1
panel_width = 900
panel_height = 34
panel_margin = 5
panel_position = bottom center

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_background = 1
panel_background_color = #000000
panel_background_alpha = 70
panel_border_width = 2
panel_border_color = #000000
panel_border_alpha = 30
panel_rounded = 18

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 110
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 2
task_icon = 1
task_icon_size = 12

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_background = 1
task_background_color = #ffffff
task_background_alpha = 40
task_active_background_color = #ffffff
task_active_background_alpha = 55

task_border_width = 1
task_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_border_alpha = 35
task_rounded = 12
task_active_border_width = 2
task_active_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_active_border_alpha = 40
task_active_rounded = 12

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION
# configure mouse action with
# (none, close, toggle, iconify, shade, toggle_iconify)
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

```

---

### Post by joninkrakow on 2008-07-15
> **Arlanthir said:**
> **Offtopic:**
Is that why it's more and more a trend at my University? -_-
I tried working with a Mac, omg, I had to go through a bunch of menus just to rename a file... I like to press F2. :(

Um, I hate to say it, but on the Mac, if the file is hilighted, you just need to hit <return> to edit the file name. No more difficult than F2. Oh, and one benefit of Mac OS is that hitting the up and down arrows while editing the file name takes you to the beginning and end of the name. 

I do thank you for the F2 trick. It works in PCMan. :-)

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-16
> **Opeth115 said:**
> really nice, i like it alot!  Would I be able to get your tint config?

Sure!

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TTM CONFIG FILE
#
# colors: hex format
# booleans: 0 or 1 
# alpha: 0 to 100 percent
# font: [FAMILY-LIST] [STYLE-OPTIONS] [SIZE]
# panel_width: 0 == use full width
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# FONT
#---------------------------------------------
font = Calibri bold 8
font_color = #ffffff
font_alpha = 200
font_active_color = #ffffff
font_active_alpha = 85
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
# panel_position : bottom left, bottom right, bottom center, top left, top right, top center
# panel_show_all_desktop = 0 : tint show one taskbar from current desktop
# panel_show_all_desktop = 1 : tint show all taskbar
#---------------------------------------------
panel_show_all_desktop = 1
panel_width = 900
panel_height = 34
panel_margin = 5
panel_position = bottom center

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_background = 1
panel_background_color = #000000
panel_background_alpha = 0
panel_border_width = 2
panel_border_color = #000000
panel_border_alpha = 0
panel_rounded = 18

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 130
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 2
task_icon = 0
task_icon_size = 12

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_background = 1
task_background_color = #ffffff
task_background_alpha = 40
task_active_background_color = #ffffff
task_active_background_alpha = 55

task_border_width = 1
task_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_border_alpha = 35
task_rounded = 5
task_active_border_width = 2
task_active_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_active_border_alpha = 40

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-16
> **71CH said:**
> Do you have any tips on setting up xfce like you have yours.

It's pretty easy, you see. What I did was to remove the taskbar from the Xfce-panel and bring it to the top. I have the main Xfce menu and the Places menu plugin. I also inserted a separator between both menus in order to have a reasonable space between them. I added another separator between Places and the tray, allowing it to expand, so that the tray and the clock applets could go to the far right of the panel. Then, using Compiz Fusion, I reduced the opacity of the panel. I still haven't found a way to make it permanent (without the taskbar, adding a special rule for the "dock" to Compiz's opacity settings does not seem to work). I just hover the panel, hold Alt and scroll down with the mouse wheel. The Xfce menu's icon is just an SVG file I have (the Unitarian flame).

For the panel's background, I inserted the following on the .gtkrc-2.0 file:

```
style "panel"
{

	bg[NORMAL] = "#ffffff"
	bg_pixmap[NORMAL] = ".background.png"
	fg[NORMAL] = "#000000"
	fg[ACTIVE] = "#ffffff"
	
}


widget_class "*Panel*" style "panel"
widget "*Panel*" style "panel"
class "*Panel*" style "panel"

```

Being .background.png the picture with the background I want, of course. It's a hidden file on my home folder.

I added Tint2 to the bottom, using the config file I quoted in a previous post. There's Conky showing what I'm listening to on MPD. And then I just applied the Aurora Aqua GTK theme and that modded version of the Eternal Fedora Emerald theme. That's pretty much it! If there's anything else I forgot to mention, please ask me. I'll be glad to help.

---

### Post by AADude on 2008-07-16
My simple xubuntu desktop:
[http://www.majhost.com/gallery/Stephens/Xubuntu/myxubuntu.png](http://www.majhost.com/gallery/Stephens/Xubuntu/myxubuntu.png)

I kinda like it. Just installed it like two days ago or so.

EDIT: By the way, this is a little script I made to help me take fast screenshots:

1.) Open Mousepad (or anything you have)
2.) Put this code in:
```
#!/bin/bash
echo ""
echo ""
echo "Screenshot filename (no extension):"
read ssfname

echo ""
echo "Taking screenshot in 5 (five) seconds..."
echo ""
echo "5 (five)"; sleep 1
echo "4 (four)"; sleep 1
echo "3 (three)"; sleep 1
echo "2 (two)"; sleep 1
echo "1 (one)"; sleep 1
echo ""
import -window root ~/$ssfname.png
echo "Screenshot saved as $ssfname.png"
echo ""
echo ""
```
3.) Save it as "ss.sh" in /home/yourname/.

Now that you're done with that, you can do this part over and over:
1.) Open Terminal
2.) Type in (and press enter):
```
bash ss.sh
```
3.) Let the script work... it will ask for the filename (without the extension) and then it will save the screenshot in "/home/yourname/" (or the current directory you're in).

You could chmod a+x ss.sh if you want to just do ./ss.sh instead of bash ss.sh.

Have fun.

### Post by urukrama on 2008-07-17
> **dbbolton said:**
> What IS she doing?

She is doing a "prostration" pilgrimage: instead of walking to the place of pilgrimage, she will take a few steps, prostrate, perhaps offer prayers, get up, take a few more steps, prostrate, etc. until her final destination. Sometimes they will do prostration circumambulations, where they will not go to a particular place, but go round a sacred site. The wood on her hands is to make it easier.

Some make it even harder and prostrate 108 times before they move on ([here]("http://www.vaisnava.cz/fotky/vrindavan/Govardhana-dandavat-baba1-v.jpg") is a picture that shows this; the beads next to the (Hindu) man are used to count the times he prostrated on that spot)

[Here]("http://www.jamd.com/search?assettype=g&assetid=52771401&text=tibet+pilgrimage"), [here]("http://www.daylife.com/photo/0fBI1zr69I3gf"), [here]("http://www.jamd.com/search?assettype=g&assetid=52771400&text=tibet+pilgrimage"), and [here]("http://www.daylife.com/photo/05l266h1T5bes") are some pictures that explain it better.

It is not an uncommon practice in Hindu and Himalayan Buddhist traditions.

EDIT: [Here]("http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/south_asia/6298729.stm") is a BBC article about the practice, and [here]("http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LzB94cDL9wM&feature=related") is a video of it in action.

---

### Post by PrimoTurbo on 2008-07-19
[[img]http://xs129.xs.to/xs129/08295/2008-07-19-001129_1280x1024_scrot420.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs129.xs.to/xs129/08295/2008-07-19-001129_1280x1024_scrot420.png)
(Click To View Bigger)

My Windows cd broke so, I decided to give Arch a try have been running it for a few days now. I wish I was running tint. But it has no pager, dock, time, volume control. The recent version is very visually appealing and very customizable, except there needs to be an option for controlling the tint of non-selected icons. It's too dark by default. I tried to setup tint, pypanel, netwmpager and to provide me with missing functionality but it's impossible to adjust many things like system tray sizing with out overlapping. Netwmpager has become annoying due to the fact that clicking a full screen app in a different desktop moves to the one you are in. For now I use lxpanel, very nice panel but visual customization is garbage, partial transparency doesn't work for some reason.

Also using a custom openbox theme I'm working on, will release at some point. Murrina-Color is the GTK and wallpaper is a new one from interfacelift.(Calm Before The Storm) Sorry for long post. :p

### Post by urukrama on 2008-07-19
Playing with [tint2]("http://code.google.com/p/tint2/")... 

I run most of my applications maximized, and have configured Openbox such that I can perform all the window actions I need to use with keybindings (so I don't really use the window decorations). 

In this setup Tint covers the window decorations of maximized windows, and creates a tab-like appearance (see second screenshot to get an idea). I quite like it.

The Gtk theme I use is my own Bygone. The Openbox theme is a modified Bygone.

### Post by spupy on 2008-07-19
I think that my desktop is approaching it's state of perfection (as perceived by me and limited by the abilities of myself and the software I use).
The idea of my desktop is similar to the one of urukrama. I use my own Fluxbox theme and a Murrine theme with modified sources, so the window and it's contents blend. When I maximize a window, the toolbar appears over the titlebar of the window and again blend with the content of the window. Also, the toolbar is invisibly shorter on the right side, so I can still click the invisible "x" to close a window. :)

Fluxbox: Sliver Aurora
Gtk: Murrine Engine with modified source code. The theme itself was Murrine Deviant some time ago.
Icons: My favorite Gnome and Tango icons.
Wallpaper: shelest.deviantart.com

[This]("http://vesso.marv.lafka.net/screens/screens24/firefox.png") is how fullscreen looks, kinda like tabs. Here are screenshots of some other programs I have customized at source code level:
[liferea]("http://vesso.marv.lafka.net/screens/screens24/mod_liferea.png")
[evince]("http://vesso.marv.lafka.net/screens/screens24/mod_evince.png")
[file-roller]("http://vesso.marv.lafka.net/screens/screens24/mod_fileroller.png")

You can also see a script I wrote - it checks my gmail account and puts the number of unread emails on the thunderbird icon in the "dock". The date icon in the dock shows the current date. :D

### Post by myusername on 2008-07-20

### Post by el mariachi on 2008-07-20
simply put: GTK themes control the appearance of the apps backgrounds, scrollbars, menubars, etc so they look more "colorful" since you are using OpenBox here's how to do it, in a nutshell:
1-go to [www.gnome-look.org](www.gnome-look.org) and download a GTK2 theme that you like
2-unpack it to ~/.themes (that's a hidden folder in your home directory), if it doesn't exist, create it.
3-install gtk-chtheme 
4-choose the theme from within gtk-chtheme
5-enjoy :D

for an awesome five-star all you can eat for free guide on openbox, just google for "urukrama", his guide is the first result (yes urukrama you're famous hehe)

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-07-20
> **el mariachi said:**
> praise Arch Linux and it's forum :lolflag:
[http://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=51282](http://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=51282)

In addition to what is said here, you don't have to use lxpanel.
Instead of lxpanel at the end of the compiz start script, you can put something like

```
while true; do sleep 10000000; done
```

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-07-20
> **el mariachi said:**
> and then we wait for the handsome prince to wake us up?

Nah, this will just make sure X keeps running.  When whatever the last line in your .xinitrc (the line with exec) ends, X dies.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-21
[[img]http://xs229.xs.to/xs229/08301/ecra526.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs229&d=08301&f=ecra526.png) [[img]http://xs329.xs.to/xs329/08301/ecra2248.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs329&d=08301&f=ecra2248.png)

Wallpaper: Aker [http://kobhen.deviantart.com/art/Aker-85575609](http://kobhen.deviantart.com/art/Aker-85575609)
GTK Theme: Dusk
Xfwm4 Theme: Ashen II
Using Tint and Trayer on the bottom of the screen and Conky on the top right corner of the screen.

To start Trayer the way I do: 

```
trayer --edge bottom --align right --widthtype request --height 18 --expand false --transparent true --alpha 255 --margin 8 --distance 8
```

My .conkyrc: 

```
# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background no

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Set conky on the bottom of all other applications
on_bottom yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont Calibri:bold:size=8

# Text alpha when using Xft
#xftalpha 0.5

# Print everything to stdout?
# out_to_console no

# MPD host/portconky
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600
# mpd_password password

# Print everything to console?
# out_to_console no

# mail spool
#mail_spool $MAIL

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 5.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
# own_window yes

# If own_window is yes, you may use type normal, desktop or overide
# own_window_type override

# Use pseudo transparency with own_window?
# own_window_transparent yes

# If own_window_transparent is set to no, you can set the background colour here
# own_window_colour white

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
own_window_hints undecorated,below,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 1000 5

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 8 no

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
#alignment none

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 30
gap_y 30

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 1

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 1

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes


# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer yes

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
${alignr}${mpd_artist} | ${mpd_title} ${font Calibri:Bold:size=22}${time %H}:${font Calibri:Bold:size=32}${time %M}${font}                               
```

My tintrc:

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TTM CONFIG FILE
#
# colors: hex format
# booleans: 0 or 1 
# alpha: 0 to 100 percent
# font: [FAMILY-LIST] [STYLE-OPTIONS] [SIZE]
# panel_width: 0 == use full width
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# FONT
#---------------------------------------------
font = Calibri bold 8
font_color = #ffffff
font_alpha = 60
font_active_color = #ffffff
font_active_alpha = 90
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
# panel_position : bottom left, bottom right, bottom center, top left, top right, top center
# panel_show_all_desktop = 0 : tint show one taskbar from current desktop
# panel_show_all_desktop = 1 : tint show all taskbar
#---------------------------------------------
panel_show_all_desktop = 1
panel_width = 1100
panel_height = 34
panel_margin = 5
panel_position = bottom center

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_background = 1
panel_background_color = #000000
panel_background_alpha = 0
panel_border_width = 2
panel_border_color = #000000
panel_border_alpha = 0
panel_rounded = 18

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 200
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 2
task_icon = 0
task_icon_size = 12

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_background = 1
task_background_color = #000000
task_background_alpha = 40
task_active_background_color = #000000
task_active_background_alpha = 55

task_border_width = 1
task_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_border_alpha = 35
task_rounded = 6
task_active_border_width = 2
task_active_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_active_border_alpha = 40
task_active_rounded = 5

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION
# configure mouse action with
# (none, close, toggle, iconify, shade, toggle_iconify)
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

```

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-21
> **myusername said:**
> how did you do that?

Well, first I removed all the other applets I had there. Next, you have to right-click on your xfce-panel and choose Customize Panel. Then slide the Transparency to 100%. Place the panel on the bottom right corner of the screen. That is important to ensure that maximized apps won't cover Tint2, which is also at the bottom of the screen (I don't know other strategies to keep it visible under Xfce). Since my Tint has a 34 pixels height, make your xfce-panel have the same size. And... That's pretty much it. Then you just have to configure Tint and Trayer. I quoted some config files some posts ago.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-21
> **myusername said:**
> cool thanks. i have never heard of tint2 before. is the configuration like conky? or is there a gui?

I quoted my tintrc (Tint2's config text file) some posts ago. But here is my current one after I modded it for this wallpaper I'm using now:

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TTM CONFIG FILE
#
# colors: hex format
# booleans: 0 or 1 
# alpha: 0 to 100 percent
# font: [FAMILY-LIST] [STYLE-OPTIONS] [SIZE]
# panel_width: 0 == use full width
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# FONT
#---------------------------------------------
font = Calibri bold 8
font_color = #ffffff
font_alpha = 60
font_active_color = #ffffff
font_active_alpha = 90
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
# panel_position : bottom left, bottom right, bottom center, top left, top right, top center
# panel_show_all_desktop = 0 : tint show one taskbar from current desktop
# panel_show_all_desktop = 1 : tint show all taskbar
#---------------------------------------------
panel_show_all_desktop = 1
panel_width = 1100
panel_height = 34
panel_margin = 5
panel_position = bottom center

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_background = 1
panel_background_color = #000000
panel_background_alpha = 0
panel_border_width = 2
panel_border_color = #000000
panel_border_alpha = 0
panel_rounded = 18

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 200
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 2
task_icon = 0
task_icon_size = 12

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_background = 1
task_background_color = #ffffff
task_background_alpha = 15
task_active_background_color = #ffffff
task_active_background_alpha = 30

task_border_width = 1
task_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_border_alpha = 0
task_rounded = 6
task_active_border_width = 2
task_active_border_color = #d2d2d2
task_active_border_alpha = 0
task_active_rounded = 5

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION
# configure mouse action with
# (none, close, toggle, iconify, shade, toggle_iconify)
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify


```

EDIT: By the way, you have to compile Tint2 in order to use it.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-22
Oh, and by the way, Tint-0.6.0 was released yesterday. It already acts like other panels do, automatically keeping a margin of the screen for itself. So there is no need to set a margin on your DE/WM settings anymore. Way cool. Tint2 is getting better and better!

[http://code.google.com/p/tint2/downloads/detail?name=tint-0.6.0.tar.gz&can=2&q=](http://code.google.com/p/tint2/downloads/detail?name=tint-0.6.0.tar.gz&can=2&q=)

### Post by andrek on 2008-07-22
> **cawill said:**

.conkyrc :
```
# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background no

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Set conky on the bottom of all other applications
on_bottom yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont Calibri:bold:size=8

# Text alpha when using Xft
#xftalpha 0.5

# Print everything to stdout?
# out_to_console no

# MPD host/portconky
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600
# mpd_password password

# Print everything to console?
# out_to_console no

# mail spool
#mail_spool $MAIL

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
# own_window yes

# If own_window is yes, you may use type normal, desktop or overide
# own_window_type override

# Use pseudo transparency with own_window?
# own_window_transparent yes

# If own_window_transparent is set to no, you can set the background colour here
# own_window_colour white

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
own_window_hints undecorated,below,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 500 5

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 8 no

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
#alignment none

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 20
gap_y 30

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 1

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 1

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes


# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer yes

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
${alignr}${mpd_artist} | ${mpd_title} ${font Calibri:Bold:size=22}
${alignr}${time %H}:${font Calibri:Bold:size=32}${time %M}${font}

```

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-07-22

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-22
> **voteforpedro36 said:**
> No, Fluxbox.

And plan B...

I never ever did what I'm about to suggest, but I googled a bit for five minutes and had an idea. How about pasting the following code into your "apps" file inside of your .fluxbox folder?

```
[app] (tint)
[sticky] {yes}
[Layer] {12}
[IconHidden] {yes}
[Deco] {NONE}
[end]
```

It is not guaranteed it will work. But try it out.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-07-23
> **RiceMonster said:**
> Giant Speck: nice wallpaper. I really like your icon theme too.

Thanks!

I altered the "Kubuntu 02" KDM theme so that it matched the color and set my wallpaper as the KDM background.  I also set my wallpaper as the background in the backgroundrc file in /etc/kde3/kdm folder.

That way, the look is seamless from the moment KDM starts to the moment my desktop loads up.

And it's really hard to find good icon themes.  I was using Buuf for a while, and despite the fact that Buuf is a really good icon theme, it just didn't match everything else on my computer.

### Post by andrek on 2008-07-23
To prevent compiz giving tint emerald's borders - open compizconfig settings manager, go to Window Decoration plugin and type > any & !type=dock into Decoration Windows box.

and regarding xfwm4.. it doesn't decorate tint's window, for me at least.

### Post by elmer_42 on 2008-07-23
> **billgoldberg said:**
> What is that movie player. Or how did you remove the borders, menu's, ...

Or is it a picture?

The bottom window is VLC (-I ncurses) and the top is feh. In openbox, you right-click and hit "Un/Decorate". For VLC, I drag the terminal that has the Ncurses UI in it to another desktop. Feh doesn't have menus to worry about, so a quick undecorate works just fine.

### Post by klange on 2008-07-24
I've taken as many steps as I possibly could to feel more at home in Windows (on a machine that has *real problems* running any Linux distro, maybe I should try a BSD or Solaris? I know Compiz runs fine under FreeBSD, etc., how's nVidia driver support?)

Clearlooks Gummy MSStyles theme (looks more clearlooks classic)
Custom made Tango theme for Firefox 3 (available as Tango 3 under experimental add-ons on the Firefox Add-Ons site)
Tango Patcher and Applications (I'm pretty close to addicted to Tango, but what I can say? It works for any theme, and any interface)
RocketDock (with a setup that very closely resembles my Cairo-Dock configuration on my server and my laptop)

GIMP, Inkscape, VLC, FF3, OOo 3.0 beta 2. Complete Cygwin installation with X often running in the background (also with Nano).

Not visible: KDE-SizerXP.exe, a small keyboard macro tool that lets me hold Alt and click to move and resize windows.



If only I could get Ubuntu, or for that matter, even just a kernel, running on this thing... I'd dual boot, though, I have some tools on here I'd rather not part with.

Anyway, two shots:

### Post by Cole on 2008-07-25
> **WindowsSucks said:**
> I've taken as many steps as I possibly could to feel more at home in Windows (on a machine that has *real problems* running any Linux distro, maybe I should try a BSD or Solaris? I know Compiz runs fine under FreeBSD, etc., how's nVidia driver support?)

Clearlooks Gummy MSStyles theme (looks more clearlooks classic)
Custom made Tango theme for Firefox 3 (available as Tango 3 under experimental add-ons on the Firefox Add-Ons site)
Tango Patcher and Applications (I'm pretty close to addicted to Tango, but what I can say? It works for any theme, and any interface)
RocketDock (with a setup that very closely resembles my Cairo-Dock configuration on my server and my laptop)

GIMP, Inkscape, VLC, FF3, OOo 3.0 beta 2. Complete Cygwin installation with X often running in the background (also with Nano).

Not visible: KDE-SizerXP.exe, a small keyboard macro tool that lets me hold Alt and click to move and resize windows.



If only I could get Ubuntu, or for that matter, even just a kernel, running on this thing... I'd dual boot, though, I have some tools on here I'd rather not part with.

Anyway, two shots:

Solaris is quite bulky, I personally don't like it (I sort of think Java defeats the whole point of using UNIX in the first place because of its baaaaad garbage collector). 

As far as BSD goes, I took some time and got it working with ZFS earlier in the year.  I had it running on gnome for a while, and it was fast and stable. :)  As far as nVidia drivers go, when I was using it there were no drivers available for 64bit BSD, but I've tried them on 32 BSD and they worked nicely.  I think it wouldn't hinder you to give BSD a shot (and try out ZFS as well :P).

### Post by voteforpedro36 on 2008-07-25
> **thil77 said:**
> > Am I the only one who notices that the active window isn't rounded in tint?

tint version ?
tint config file ?


```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = single_desktop
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom_left
panel_size = 1280 17
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 0 0
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 0
panel_border_width = 2
panel_background_color = #D03613 0
panel_border_color = #000000 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 155
task_margin = 15
task_padding = 0
task_icon_size = 0
task_font = nu 7
task_font_color = #FFFFFF 100
task_active_font_color = #D03613 100

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 280
task_background_color = #D03613 100
task_active_background_color = #FFFFFF 100
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #000000 0
task_active_border_color = #000000 100

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format =%H:%M %B %d
time1_font = nu 7
#time2_format = %A %B %d
time2_font = nu 6
clock_font_color = #D03613 100

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = toggle_iconify
mouse_scroll_up = toggle_iconify
mouse_scroll_down = toggle_iconify



```

It's the latest version of tint.

### Post by RiceMonster on 2008-07-26
> **nycste said:**
> i have plenty of power on my computer so using such lightweight window managers i kept asking myself why bother... i suppose if i can find benefits to using them then i say bye bye to gnome and nautilus right?

I thought the same at first; I have 2GB ram and a 1.7GHZ dualcore processor. I can run GNOME or KDE nice and fast, but I prefer a lightweight window manager because I find them more configurable, and they don't come with stuff I don't want like GNOME and KDE do.

> **nycste said:**
> im a full xp user up to a week ago, and now im 1 week into linux fully. simple things drive me crazy and i wanna just mention 2 of them again this is my xp mindset that has been drilled in me since 2001 i think
Understandable. Be patient though, you'll learn to adjust. I was the same at first as well.


> **nycste said:**
> 1. i dont understand how its 2008 and howmany modifications later why cant gnome or nautilus properly space icons on the desktop... its mind boggling to me and drives me nuts, the spacing and fonts and all that stuff just always messup, and then when you mount things or something icons overlap and stuff and wow its soo annoying

Don't use desktop icons, they make everything look messy, and they're pointless. That's just my opinion though.

> **nycste said:**
> 2. im used to using list and details folder view in xp, well in hardy ubuntu gnome nautilus i have only 2 options that im aware of, icons and list well icon view is fine if you like that i personally dont at all but the list option after being used to xp is horrible.

Give KDE a try, Konqueror's got list and details views. That's the default file manager and web browser for KDE 3.5, by the way.

If some things about GNOME bug you, give KDE or Xfce a try, or if you're brave enough yet, a lightweight window manager. They might be better suited for you.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-07-26
> **cawill said:**
> Nice, how did you achieve that?
Shell is Black Box Lean for Windows. Tango Patcher gets rid of the default explorer icons. As Windows seems to handle dark bitmap system themes badly, though, I've just used the old Windows 9X shell style and modified the colours via regedit; doesn't look pretty but it gets the job done.
> **nycste said:**
> 1. i dont understand how its 2008 and howmany modifications later why cant gnome or nautilus properly space icons on the desktop... its mind boggling to me and drives me nuts, the spacing and fonts and all that stuff just always messup, and then when you mount things or something icons overlap and stuff and wow its soo annoying I'm not sure I understand the problem. What happens when you mount a volume? it's been a year or so since I've used nautilus for the desktop but there's no option to align icons to a grid? 

> 2. im used to using list and details folder view in xp, well in hardy ubuntu gnome nautilus i have only 2 options that im aware of, icons and list well icon view is fine if you like that i personally dont at all but the list option after being used to xp is horrible. 

the list in xp was great, simple to the point no different colors and stuff the list in ubuntu is trying to be details but fails hard. details in xp is great and actually tells you the full details of files and the full size of them which ubuntu doesnt, 

can i make ubuntu show me 9478 KB instead of the default metho id shows in list 9.3MB id just like to see more detailed settings Without changing your whole desktop environment, there are a couple of different file managers to consider trying: Thunar and PCManFM. You'll find both in the software repositories so it's simply a matter of opening up synaptic and searching for them.

Failing that, KDE is a more powerful desktop environment and it's two major file managers; Konqueror and Dolphin, both give you a lot of customisation options.

### Post by urukrama on 2008-07-26
> **Yes said:**
> What line did you use to open 9menu?  Whenever I try opening it 9menu says that it can't find the font.

I'm not sure what rjmdomingo is using, but I use the following:

```
9menu -popup -bg "#000000" -fg "#F2EDD7" -font "-*-nu-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*" -teleport -file /home/urukrama/.9menurc
```

You need to give a full X11 font string. You can find those with xfontsel (which should be installed by default on your computer).

---

### Post by BwackNinja on 2008-07-26
Here's my desktop:

I'm using a modified version of the default intrepid theme NewHuman (#272727 for the window background, the darkest color that doesn't cause OOo to use the high contrast inverse icons).

Background taken shamelessly from: [http://ncarboni.home.att.net/Astrophotography.html](http://ncarboni.home.att.net/Astrophotography.html)

Emerald decorations made myself (the default metacity window decorations were too plain for me, I can upload if anyone cares).

Icons are Gray-ce-ful.

Conky is modified/compiled from a few different sources (can also upload if anyone wants it).

[[IMG]http://h1.ripway.com/NoOne100/Images/IntrepidThemeSmall.png[/IMG]]("http://h1.ripway.com/NoOne100/Images/IntrepidTheme.png")

### Post by markp1989 on 2008-07-27
I decided to go for the minimal approach 

OS: Ubuntu Hardy 64bit
Window Manager: Compiz stand alone
GTK: Crude
emerald: made by me
Icon: blackwhite 2
Dock: Fbpanel

firefox changed using this guide [http://wiki.eeeuser.com/howto:shrinkfirefox](http://wiki.eeeuser.com/howto:shrinkfirefox)

Edit: Does any one know why in the second screen shot my conky looks like that?

there is my conky rc 

```
background yes
font Sans:size=8
#xftfont Sans:size=10
use_xft yes
xftalpha 0.9
update_interval 1
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 220 5
maximum_width 220
draw_shades yes
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes
default_color white
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color green
alignment top_right
gap_x 5
gap_y 30
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
uppercase yes # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase

TEXT
${color white}SYSTEM ${hr 1}${color}
Hostname: $alignr$nodename
Arch: $alignr$machine
Kernel: $alignr$kernel
Uptime: $alignr$uptime
CPU Temp: ${alignr}${acpitemp}C

CPU INFO:${hr 1} 
Speed:     ${alignr}${freq_dyn} GHz
Temp:      ${alignr}${acpitemp} C
Processes: ${alignr}$processes ($running_processes running)
Load:      ${alignr}$cpu  %
${cpubar cpu0 4}

Video Card:${hr 1}
GPU Temp:     ${alignr}${execi 30 nvclock -T | grep GPU | cut -c20-22}°C
Video RAM:    ${alignr}${execi 30 nvclock -i | grep 'Amount:' | cut -c10-15} ${execi 30 nvclock -i | grep 'Type:' | cut -c16-20}
Memory Clock: ${alignr}${alignr}${execi 30 nvclock -i | grep 'Clock:' | cut -c10-20}
GPU Clock:    ${alignr}${execi 30 nvclock -i | grep 'GPU clock:' | cut -c13-23}


Highest CPU $alignr CPU% MEM%
${top name 1}$alignr${top cpu 1}${top mem 1}
${top name 2}$alignr${top cpu 2}${top mem 2}
${top name 3}$alignr${top cpu 3}${top mem 3}

Highest MEM $alignr CPU% MEM%
${top_mem name 1}$alignr${top_mem cpu 1}${top_mem mem 1}
${top_mem name 2}$alignr${top_mem cpu 2}${top_mem mem 2}
${top_mem name 3}$alignr${top_mem cpu 3}${top_mem mem 3}

Ram ${alignr}$mem / $memmax ($memperc%)
${membar 4}

${color white}Filesystem ${hr 1}${color}
Root: ${alignr}${fs_used /} / ${fs_size /}
${fs_bar 4 /}
Home: ${alignr}${fs_used /home} / ${fs_size /home}
${fs_bar 4 /home}
Data: ${alignr}${fs_used /media/data} / ${fs_size /media/data}
${fs_bar 4 /media/data}
Downloads: ${alignr}${fs_used /media/downloads} / ${fs_size /media/downloads}
${fs_bar 4 /media/downloads}
RAMDISK: ${alignr}${fs_used /media/rd} / ${fs_size /media/rd}
${fs_bar 4 /media/rd}

${color white}NETWORK ${hr 1}${color}
LAN IP: ${addr eth0}
Down ${downspeed eth0} k/s ${alignr}Up ${upspeed eth0} k/s
${downspeedgraph eth0 25,107} ${alignr}${upspeedgraph eth0 25,107}
Total ${totaldown eth0} ${alignr}Total ${totalup eth0}



```

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-27
> **wersdaluv said:**
> Glow is great! Aurora's goodness minus all its badness! You managed to fix it with the good stuff from other engines. OpenOffice.org doesn't look terrible with Aurora anymore.

It's just that, I still find this theme heavy like other Aurora themes and I miss the window list of Aurora. 

Genius!

Thanks for the compliments and for understanding the concept of the theme!... I used Murrine for the window list because, in the desktop environment I use, Xfce, Aurora looks odd in the Xfce-panel: either the buttons get too tight, and if I increase the size of the panel it's the tray icons which get all over the place. And besides, the window list buttons in the Xfce-panel do not have the same behavior than in GNOME. So I decided to go in a cleaner direction and try out Murrine (which I seldom like to use in my desktop, but I liked the effect of that particular element).

I never really noticed how some engines seem slower than others (except perhaps for the pixmap themes, I guess). How exactly can one measure which engine is faster than others? Any specific tool or?...

### Post by Lod on 2008-07-27
I was wondering. I see a lot of screenshots with people having their applicationsmenu somewhere on the desktop. I gather this is called up with the right mousebutton. I know this can be done in WM like xfce and fluxbox, is it possible to have something like that in Gnome?

---

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-07-27
> **Lod said:**
> I was wondering. I see a lot of screenshots with people having their applicationsmenu somewhere on the desktop. I gather this is called up with the right mousebutton. I know this can be done in WM like xfce and fluxbox, is it possible to have something like that in Gnome?

I use openbox, and you can use it with GNOME instead of metacity or compiz.  If you told nautilus not to draw the desktop, you could have openbox's menu on the desktop.

Alternatively, you can remove the menu (Applications, Places, System or the GNOME foot) from your panels and then press Alt + F1 to have the menu come up at your mouse cursor.  Not quite the same as a right click, but it would look the same in a screenshot at least.

---

### Post by schauerlich on 2008-07-27
> **dbbolton said:**
> Oops, I meant "Isn't OS X beta the same thing as 10.5?". If you google "os x beta", Leopard's homepage is the first result.

The OS X beta was just that... a beta of OS X. It was the prerelease version floating around before OS X v10.0 was released and preinstalled on machines. 10.5 is the 6th major release since then. It's the difference between the very first Ubuntu betas and 8.04.

### Post by the8thstar on 2008-07-28
Updated from last post. The bars and the background have changed.

Font: Liberation Sans size 9 for everything (except terminal) with hinting and LCD enabled - I receommend it highly because of its very good visibility
Gtk: Clearlooks-classic
Metacity: ooboontoo-mgs, inverted to match OS X button distribution on the bar
Dock: AWN 
Icons: Oxygen-refit-orange
Background: bytes_01_17_Artis_Zeego.jpg
Bar image: modded, available below

All themes and images are available through Google.

### Post by Lod on 2008-07-29
> **jordanmthomas said:**
> I use openbox, and you can use it with GNOME instead of metacity or compiz.  If you told nautilus not to draw the desktop, you could have openbox's menu on the desktop.

Alternatively, you can remove the menu (Applications, Places, System or the GNOME foot) from your panels and then press Alt + F1 to have the menu come up at your mouse cursor.  Not quite the same as a right click, but it would look the same in a screenshot at least.Thanks, I never noticed Openbox before but it seems very nice. I'm looking for something like this because I like a minimalistic desktop. Less is more.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-07-29
> **cardinals_fan said:**
> A light Xfce with a custom wallpaper.  I like desert photos more though.

[[IMG]http://c.imagehost.org/t/0495/2008-07-29-131657_1280x1024_scrot.jpg[/IMG]](http://c.imagehost.org/view/0495/2008-07-29-131657_1280x1024_scrot.png)

Could you share your .conkyrc with us, please? Thanks in advance.

[QUOTE=KneeTie]very nice setup , would like to know what you use on the bottom , the taskbar and the tray , and if they use config files what they are ,Thx in advance.[/QUOTE]

On that screenshot, I was using Tint2 and Trayer.

My tintrc from back then:

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = multi_monitor
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom center
panel_size = 1110 34
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 5 3
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 9
panel_border_width = 2
panel_background_color = #000000 0
panel_border_color = #000000 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 200
task_margin = 5
task_padding = 2
task_icon_size = 0
task_font = Calibri bold 8
task_font_color = #ffffff 75
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 90

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 3
task_background_color = #ffffff 25
task_active_background_color = #ef3117 85
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #ffffff 0
task_active_border_color = #ffffff 0

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
#time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = Calibri bold 12
#time2_format = %A %d %B
time2_font = Calibri bold 8
clock_font_color = #ffffff 76

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify


```


To start Trayer, I use the following command:

```
trayer --edge bottom --align right --widthtype request --height 18 --expand false --transparent true --alpha 255 --margin 8 --distance 8
```
